The Distinction Between Linguistic and Ontological Making
Specifying that the dispute concerns ontological making and presenting the core argument with the dyer analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between linguistic making (al-ja'l al-lughawi) and ontological making, and how the agent's effect relates to the essence with respect to existence, using the dyer analogy.

Core Idea
The dispute is about real making, not linguistic; the agent makes the essence existent, but not the essence itself.

In this passage, Sanusi specifies that the debate about whether essences are 'made' concerns ontological making, not the everyday linguistic use. He argues that the essence itself cannot be made because there is no distinction between it and itself. The example of the dyer dyeing a garment illustrates how an agent affects an essence without making the essence itself. This lesson unpacks that core argument and the dyer analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Focus on the opening statement that the dispute is not about linguistic making. Then follow the argument that there is no distinction between the essence and itself.
2
Understand the no-distinction argument
The text argues that since there is no distinction between the essence and itself, no making can be conceived that would make the essence itself. Understand why this precludes direct making.
3
Analyze the dyer analogy
The dyer does not make the garment or the dye, but makes the garment qualified by the dye. Similarly, the agent makes the essence existent, not the essence itself. See the parallel.
The key point: the effect is the essence-with-respect-to-existence.
4
Conclude the meaning of 'making'
The passage concludes that essences in themselves are not made, nor are their existences; what is made is the essence in its being existent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( أن معنى قولهم إلخ) يعني أن معنى قولهم : إنها مجعولة ظاهر، وهو الاحتياج إلى الموجد لا يحتاج إلى التعرض ومعنى قولهم الماهيات غير مجعولة أنها ليست نفسها ولا جزءها، وإنما كان أبعد لاشتراكه مع ما قاله المصنف في أنه ليس للتخصيص كثير فائدة، يرد عليه أن هذا الحكم قد علم من قولهم : وهي مغايرة لما عداها بأبلغ بيان فالتعرض له مستدرك ولأنه لا وجه حينئذ لمذهب التفصيل. وما قيل من أنه على هذا ينبغي أن يحمل قولهم : غير مجعولة على السلب ففيه أنه على جميع الوجوه المذكورة محمولة على السلب كما لا يخفى . قوله : ( ولا تأثير (مؤثر) أشار بالعطف إلى أن النزاع ليس في الجعل اللغوي، فإنه يستعمل بمعنى الخلق والصيرورة والتصيير، ومعنى طفق . قوله : (إن المجعولية ليست نفس الماهية الخ) فقولهم الماهية غير مجعولة ينبغي أن يحمل حينئذ على السلب لا العدول كما هو ظاهر العبارة؛ لأن الماهية من حيث هي ليست غير معها مفهوماً سواها، لم يعقل هناك جعل، إذ لا مغايرة بين الماهية ونفسها حتى يتصور توسط جعل جاعل بينهما، فتكون إحداهما مجعولة تلك الأخرى. وكذا لا يتصور تأثير الفاعل في الوجود بمعني جعل الوجود وجوداً ، بل تأثيره في الماهية باعتبار الوجود، بمعنى أنه يجعلها متصفة بالوجود، لا بمعنى أنه يجعل اتصافها موجوداً متحققاً في الخارج، فإن الصباغ مثلاً إذا صبغ ثوباً، فإنه لا يجعل الثوب ثوباً، ولا الصبغ صبغا، بل يجعل الثوب متصفا بالصبغ في الخارج وإن لم يجعل اتصافه به موجوداً ثابتاً في الخارج، فليست الماهيات في أنفسها مجعولةً، ولا وجوداتها أيضاً في أنفسها مجعولة، بل الماهيات في كونها موجودة مجعولة وهذا المعنى مما لا قوله : (إذ لا مغايرة إلخ) فيه بحث؛ لأن هذا إنما يفيد عدم تعلق الجعل بالسواد بمعنى جعل شيء شيئاً؛ ولا يفيد نفي تعلق الجعل به بأن يكون نفسه أثر الفاعل وتابعاً للجعل، ومعنى التأثير استتباع المؤثر الأثر، لا ما يتبادر إلى الوهم، أعني إيجاد الأثر. قوله : ( وكذا إلخ ) هذه المقدمة لا دخل لها في بيان أنها ليست بمجعولة، بل توطئة لبيان معنى الجعل، ودفع لما مر من أنه إذا لم تكن ماهية ما مجعولة انتفى المجعولية بالكلية؛ لأن كل ما يفرض تعلق الجعل به من الوجود والموصوفية فهو ماهية في نفسه قوله: (بمعنى جعل الوجود وجوداً) وكذا في الاتصاف بمعنى جعل الاتصاف اتصافاً. قوله : (بل تأثيره إلخ) فالأثر هي الماهية باعتبار الوجود فيتصور توسط الجعل بينهما، بأن يقال : جعل الماهية موجودة، وليس الأثر الاتصاف حتى يرد أنكم قد اعترفتم يكون الاتصاف أثر الفاعل بنفسه، فلم لا تقولون الماهيات كلها كذلك ؟ وأن الأثر هو الأمر الخارجي، والاتصاف ليس كذلك. قوله: (لا) بمعنى أنه يجعل إلخ) فإن الاتصاف إنما يكون موجوداً إذا كان الخارج ظرفاً لوجوده، وفيما نحن فيه الخارج ظرف لنفسه قوله : ( فإن الصباغ إلخ ) تصوير للمعقول بالمحسوس لإيضاحه . قوله : ( وهذا المعنى إلخ فيه بحث؛ لأن ما ذكره إنما يصح إذا كان الاتصاف بالوجود حقيقياً بأن يكون الوجود أمراً زائداً على الماهية تتصف الماهية به سواء كان الوجود موجوداً بنفسه أو معدوماً. وقد عرفت بطلانه بناء على ما هو المشهور من أن ثبوت شيء لشيء فرع لثبوت المثبت له، إلا أن يقال باستثناء الوجود عنه، كما ذهب إليه الإمام، أو يقال بالاستلزام دون الفرعية، كما ذهب إليه المحقق الدواني. أما إذا كان انتزاعياً محضاً؛ ولا يكون في الخارج إلا الماهية ، فلا معنى لقوله بأنه يجعلها متصفة بالوجود. مجعولة أيضاً، على معنى أن اللامجعولية ليست نفسها ولا داخلة فيها. ووجه الأبعدية مع استوائهما في انتفاء وجه تخصيص هذا البحث بالمجعولية؛ أنه على هذا كان معلوماً في أول بحث الماهية، فلا وجه لذكره ثانياً كما هو دأبهم .
His statement: 'That the meaning of their statement, etc.' means that the meaning of their statement 'it is made' is apparent, namely the need for the creator, which does not need to be addressed. And the meaning of their statement 'essences are not made' is that they are not themselves nor a part of it [i.e., the being-made]. And it was only more distant (ab'ad) because it shares with what the author said in that there is not much benefit in specification. It is objected to him that this judgment has been learned from their statement 'and they are different from what is other than them' with the most eloquent expression, so addressing it is redundant, and because there is then no scope for the doctrine of detail (madhhab al-tafsil). And what is said that on this basis their statement 'not made' should be interpreted as negation (salb), then it is that in all the mentioned aspects it is interpreted as negation, as is not hidden. His statement: 'And no effect of an agent' — he indicated by the conjunction that the dispute is not about linguistic making (al-ja'l al-lughawi), for it is used in the meaning of creation, making, and rendering, and the meaning of 'tafiqa' (began). His statement: 'Indeed, being-made is not the essence itself, etc.' — so their statement 'the essence is not made' should then be interpreted as negation, not as the more common (al-'udul), as is apparent from the expression; because the essence, inasmuch as it is, is not along with it a concept other than it; no making is conceived there, since there is no distinction between the essence and itself such that a maker's making could be imagined between them, so that one of them would be made of the other. Likewise, the agent's effect is not conceived in existence in the sense of making existence an existence; rather his effect is on the essence with respect to existence, in the sense that he makes it qualified by existence, not in the sense that he makes its qualification existent and realized in the external. For example, if a dyer dyes a garment, he does not make the garment a garment, nor the dye dye, but he makes the garment qualified by the dye in the external, even if he does not make its qualification by it existent and fixed in the external. So essences in themselves are not made, nor are their existences in themselves made; rather essences in their being existent are made. And this meaning is something which... His statement: 'Since there is no distinction, etc.' — there is discussion in it; because this only proves the non-attachment of making to blackness in the sense of making one thing another; but it does not prove the negation of the attachment of making to it by its being itself the effect of the agent and subsequent to the making. And the meaning of effect (al-ta'thir) is the agent's bringing about of the effect, not what comes to mind, namely the bringing into existence of the effect. His statement: 'And likewise, etc.' — this premise has no role in explaining that it is not made; rather it is a preparation for explaining the meaning of making, and for repelling what has passed that if a certain essence is not made, then being-made is negated entirely; because everything to which making is supposed to attach, from existence and being-qualified, is itself an essence. His statement: 'In the sense of making existence an existence' — and likewise in qualification, in the sense of making qualification a qualification. His statement: 'Rather his effect, etc.' — so the effect is the essence with respect to existence, so the intermediation of making between them is conceived, such that it is said: He made the essence existent. And the effect is not the qualification, so that it might be objected that you have admitted that the qualification is the effect of the agent itself, so why do you not say that all essences are likewise? And that the effect is the external thing, and the qualification is not so. His statement: 'No, in the sense that he makes, etc.' — for the qualification is only existent when the external is the locus of its existence, and in our case the external is the locus of itself. His statement: 'For the dyer, etc.' — is a depiction of the intelligible by the sensible to clarify it. His statement: 'And this meaning, etc.' — there is discussion in it; because what he mentioned is only valid if the qualification by existence is real (haqiqi), such that existence is something additional to the essence, the essence is qualified by it, whether existence is existent by itself or non-existent. And you have known its falsehood based on what is well-known that the subsistence of a thing for a thing is branch of the subsistence of the subject of attribution, unless it is said that existence is excepted from this, as the Imam held, or it is said by way of implication (al-istilzam) without branch-subordination, as al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawwani held. But if it is purely derivative (intiza'i), and there is nothing in the external except the essence, then there is no meaning to his saying that he makes it qualified by existence. Also, it is not made, in the sense that the non-being-made (al-lamaj'uliyya) is not itself nor part of it. And the reason for its being more distant (al-ab'adiyya), while they are equal in the negation of a specific aspect for this investigation on being-made, is that on this it would have been known at the beginning of the investigation of essence, so there is no reason to mention it a second time, as is their custom.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This lengthy passage delves into the precise meaning of 'the essence is not made.' It begins by clarifying that the meaning of 'the essence is made' is simply the need for a creator, while 'not made' means that the essence itself is not the act of making nor a part of it. The claim that this interpretation is 'more distant' (ab'ad) is examined and objected to. The passage then discusses that the dispute is not about linguistic making but about ontological making. It argues that since there is no distinction between the essence and itself, no making can be conceived that would make the essence itself. The agent's effect is on the essence with respect to existence: he makes the essence existent, not the existence itself. The analogy of the dyer illustrates this: the dyer makes the garment dyed, not the garment or the dye. Therefore, essences in themselves are not made, nor are their existences; rather what is made is the essence in its being existent. Subsequent objections are addressed: the objection that if essences are not made, then nothing is made, is answered by stating that the effect is the essence with respect to existence, and making is conceived between them. The passage concludes with a discussion on the nature of existence and qualification, noting that if existence is purely derivative (intiza'i), then the statement that the agent makes the essence qualified by existence has no meaning.

Key Terms
جعل (making)
تأثير (effect)
صباغ (dyer)
اتصاف (qualification)
وجود (existence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the agent makes the essence itself or the existence itself directly.
Correction: The passage explains that the agent makes the essence existent, not the essence itself nor existence itself. The effect is on the essence with respect to existence.

Checkpoint
According to the dyer analogy, what does the dyer do?
A) He makes the garment.
B) He makes the dye.
C) He makes the garment qualified by the dye.
D) He makes both the garment and the dye.

Key Takeaway
Essences are not made in themselves; only the essence in its being existent is made, just as a dyer makes a garment dyed, not the garment or the dye.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you claim to 'make' something in your daily life (a decision, an action, a creation), do you recognize that you never make the essence of things—only their state of being? How does this truth reshape your understanding of your own agency and creativity? Before your next action, pause and ask: 'Am I acting as if I create from nothing, or as one who merely qualifies what already exists?' Commit to tracing every effect back to the Real Agent (Allah).
?
If your very essence is not 'made' by you or any creature, then your identity is a given—a trust. Are you living as though your essence is a gift from Allah, or do you behave as if you own your own essence and can redefine it at will? How must you change your self-perception today to align with this lesson? Write one concrete step to remind yourself that your essence is not self-made.
?
The dyer does not make the garment or the dye; he only makes the garment dyed. Similarly, your actions do not create new essences—they only qualify what already is. Does this humble you to see that even your best deeds are not truly 'yours'? Are you willing to attribute every good quality in your character not to your own making but to Allah's making you qualified by it? Pray for the grace to live with that awareness.

Causality and Created Things
advanced
8 min
Objections and Responses on the Making of Essences
Addressing objections and refining the concept of making and effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key objections to the claim that essences are not made, and how the author defends his position by clarifying the meaning of effect and the role of existence.

Core Idea
If essences are not made, what is? The answer: the essence in its existence is made, and the effect is the essence in that state.

After presenting the core position, the text addresses several objections. One questions the no-distinction argument, another asks if nothing would be made if essences themselves are not made. The author responds by refining the concept of 'effect' and 'making', arguing that the effect is the essence with respect to existence, and that the maker's role is to make the essence existent, not to make the essence itself. This lesson walks through these objections and their resolutions.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections and responses
The passage contains several objections. Start with the first: the no-distinction argument only negates one kind of making, not all. Then the second: if no essence is made, then nothing is made.
2
Understand the clarification of 'effect' (ta'thir)
The text redefines 'effect' as the agent's bringing about of the effect, not the popular understanding of creating the effect. This resolves the objection.
3
Analyze the response to the 'nothing made' objection
The response states that the effect is the essence with respect to existence, not the qualification itself. The essence in that state is made.
4
Grasp the final discussion on the nature of existence
The passage ends with a discussion on whether qualification by existence is real or derivative. Understand the implications for the dyer analogy.

بالمحسوس لإيضاحه . قوله : ( وهذا المعنى إلخ فيه بحث؛ لأن ما ذكره إنما يصح إذا كان الاتصاف بالوجود حقيقياً بأن يكون الوجود أمراً زائداً على الماهية تتصف الماهية به سواء كان الوجود موجوداً بنفسه أو His statement: 'That the meaning of their statement, etc.' means that the meaning of their statement 'it is made' is apparent, namely the need for the creator, which does not need to be addressed. And the meaning of their statement 'essences are not made' is that they are not themselves nor a part of it [i.e., the being-made]. His statement: 'Since there is no distinction, etc.' — there is discussion in it; because this only proves the non-attachment of making to blackness in the sense of making one thing another; but it does not prove the negation of the attachment of making to it by its being itself the effect of the agent and subsequent to the making. And the meaning of effect (al-ta'thir) is the agent's bringing about of the effect, not what comes to mind, namely the bringing into existence of the effect. His statement: 'And likewise, etc.' — this premise has no role in explaining that it is not made; rather it is a preparation for explaining the meaning of making, and for repelling what has passed that if a certain essence is not made, then being-made is negated entirely; because everything to which making is supposed to attach, from existence and being-qualified, is itself an essence. His statement: 'In the sense of making existence an existence' — and likewise in qualification, in the sense of making qualification a qualification. His statement: 'Rather his effect, etc.' — so the effect is the essence with respect to existence, so the intermediation of making between them is conceived, such that it is said: He made the essence existent. And the effect is not the qualification, so that it might be objected that you have admitted that the qualification is the effect of the agent itself, so why do you not say that all essences are likewise? And that the effect is the external thing, and the qualification is not so. His statement: 'No, in the sense that he makes, etc.' — for the qualification is only existent when the external is the locus of its existence, and in our case the external is the locus of itself. His statement: 'For the dyer, etc.' — is a depiction of the intelligible by the sensible to clarify it. His statement: 'And this meaning, etc.' — there is discussion in it; because what he mentioned is only valid if the qualification by existence is real (haqiqi), such that existence is something additional to the essence, the essence is qualified by it, whether existence is existent by itself or non-existent. And you have known its falsehood based on what is well-known that the subsistence of a thing for a thing is branch of the subsistence of the subject of attribution, unless it is said that existence is excepted from this, as the Imam held, or it is said by way of implication (al-istilzam) without branch-subordination, as al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawwani held. But if it is purely derivative (intiza'i), and there is nothing in the external except the essence, then there is no meaning to his saying that he makes it qualified by existence. Also, it is not made, in the sense that the non-being-made (al-lamaj'uliyya) is not itself nor part of it. And the reason for its being more distant (al-ab'adiyya), while they are equal in the negation of a specific aspect for this investigation on being-made, is that on this it would have been known at the beginning of the investigation of essence, so there is no reason to mention it a second time, as is their custom.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This lengthy passage delves into the precise meaning of 'the essence is not made.' It begins by clarifying that the meaning of 'the essence is made' is simply the need for a creator, while 'not made' means that the essence itself is not the act of making nor a part of it. The claim that this interpretation is 'more distant' (ab'ad) is examined and objected to. The passage then discusses that the dispute is not about linguistic making but about ontological making. It argues that since there is no distinction between the essence and itself, no making can be conceived that would make the essence itself. The agent's effect is on the essence with respect to existence: he makes the essence existent, not the existence itself. The analogy of the dyer illustrates this: the dyer makes the garment dyed, not the garment or the dye. Therefore, essences in themselves are not made, nor are their existences; rather what is made is the essence in its being existent. Subsequent objections are addressed: the objection that if essences are not made, then nothing is made, is answered by stating that the effect is the essence with respect to existence, and making is conceived between them. The passage concludes with a discussion on the nature of existence and qualification, noting that if existence is purely derivative (intiza'i), then the statement that the agent makes the essence qualified by existence has no meaning.

Key Terms
تأثير (effect)
اتصاف (qualification)
انتزاعي (derivative)
حقيقي (real)
وجود (existence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that if essences are not made, then nothing is made at all.
Correction: The author clarifies that what is made is the essence in its state of being existent, not the essence itself. So making does occur, just not on the pure essence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect (al-athar) of the agent?
A) The existence itself.
B) The qualification (al-ittisaf) of the essence by existence.
C) The essence with respect to existence.
D) The essence itself.

Key Takeaway
The effect of the maker is the essence with respect to existence, making it existent, not the essence itself or existence alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When you contemplate your own existence, do you ever think that Allah not only brought you from nothing but also gives you your specific essence and qualities each moment? How does that awareness change the way you live today?
?
The lesson distinguishes between making an essence and making it existent. In your daily actions, do you sometimes focus on 'what' you are doing (the essence) and forget that the very ability to act is an existence given by Allah? What would it mean for you to orient your intention towards Him in that gift?
?
This passage debates whether qualification by existence is real or derivative. When you describe yourself as 'believer' or 'sinner', do you treat those as fixed essences or as contingent states constantly sustained by Allah? Which view leads to greater humility and reliance on Him?

Refuting the Mental vs. External Commonality Objection
Refutes objection that commonality is only mental and defends essential attributes as intrinsic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that commonality is only mental is refuted by demonstrating that essential predicates like humanity are not mere accidents but are rooted in the essence itself.

Core Idea
Essential predicates are not added by a separate cause; they are the very making of the essence.

In this passage, the author addresses a subtle objection: if commonality among individuals is only mental, then it cannot prove external ta'ayyun. But if it is external, it is denied by those who claim natures are mere abstractions. Al-Dawani refutes this by showing that if essential predicates were merely caused, then Zayd would not be essentially human, leading to an absurd regress. The author then reinforces this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
The passage contains an objection, a refutation by al-Dawani, and the author's own comment.
2
Identify the two interpretations of 'sharing'
The objection presents two possibilities: sharing in the mind or sharing externally. Understand why each is problematic.
The author refutes both, but focuses on the external denial by those who deny natures.
3
Analyze al-Dawani's argument
Al-Dawani argues that if Zayd were not essentially human, he would need a separate cause for his humanity, which is absurd. This shows that essential predicates are not mere accidents.
The argument uses reductio ad absurdum.
4
Understand the author's own point
The author adds that if mental concepts are abstracted from the same thing, they cannot be denied of it, and their making is the making of the essence.
This reinforces that essential attributes are not additional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقي هاهنا بحث وهو أنه إن أراد بقوله : أنها متشاركة في شيء اشتراكها في الذهن فلا يجدي؛ لأنه لا يلزم منه وجود التعين في الخارج. وإن أراد اشتراكها في الخارج فممنوع فإن من ينفي وجود الطبائع يقول إن الأشخاص أمور بسيطة، والطبائع والتشخصات أمور انتزاعية إلا أن ما ينتزع من نفس الأشخاص يسمى ذاتيات، وما ينتزع عنها باعتبار اكتنافها بالعوارض يسمى عرضيات وقد تصدى لدفعه المحقق الدواني فقال : لو كان الأمر كذلك لم يكن زيد في حد ذاته إنساناً ولا حيواناً ولا ناطقاً؛ لما علم أن الماهية من حيث هي ليست إلا الماهية وذلك يستلزم أن يكون اتصافه المفهومات بجميع الكلية معللة بعلة كما هو شأن اللواحق، فيكون زيد كما يحتاج إلى جاعل يجعله أبيض يحتاج إلى جاعل يجعله إنساناً؛ بأن يتوسط الجعل بينه وبين الإنسان؛ إذ المفروض أنه في ذاته أمر آخر. أقول : إذا كان الذهنيات منتزعة من نفس الشيء تكون كلها في مرتبة، فكيف يمكن سلبها عنه، وكيف يحتاج إلى جاعل يجعله موصوفاً بتلك الذاتيات ولذا قالوا: إن جعلها جعل الذات ووجوده وجودها، وقد مر ذلك
There remains a discussion here, namely: if by his statement 'that they share in something' he means their sharing in the mind, then it is of no use, because the existence of ta'ayyun externally does not follow from it. And if he means their sharing externally, then it is denied, for those who deny the existence of natures say that persons are simple things, and natures and individuations are abstracted matters, except that what is abstracted from the persons themselves is called essential, and what is abstracted from them by virtue of their being surrounded by accidents is called accidental. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani set out to refute this, saying: If that were the case, then Zayd would not in his very essence be human, nor animal, nor rational; because it is known that the essence insofar as it is essence is nothing but the essence, and that would necessitate that his being described by all universal concepts is caused by a cause, as is the case with concomitants. Then Zayd would need, just as he needs a maker to make him white, he would need a maker to make him human, by making the making intermediate between him and humanity, since it is supposed that in himself he is something else. I say: If the mental concepts are abstracted from the thing itself, they are all on the same level, so how can they be denied of it? And how does he need a maker to make him described by those essentials? Therefore they said: Their making is the making of the essence, and their existence is its existence. And this has been mentioned.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection regarding whether the commonality among individuals is mental or external. The objection states: if the commonality is only mental, then it does not prove ta'ayyun in external existence. If it is external, it is denied by those who deny natures; they claim persons are simple and natures and individuations are merely conceptual abstractions. Al-Dawani refutes this by arguing that if Zayd's essential predicates (human, animal, rational) were merely accidental or added by a cause, then he would not be essentially human; he would need a separate maker to make him human, just as he needs a maker to make him white. This is absurd because these are essential, not accidental. The author then adds that if mental concepts are abstracted from the same thing, they are all in the same rank, so they cannot be denied of the thing. The conclusion is that the making of these essentials is the making of the essence itself, not an additional act.

Correction: They are intrinsic to the essence; the 'making' of the essence itself is what these predications refer to.

Key Takeaway
Essential predicates like humanity are not accidental additions but constitutive of the essence itself, so their 'making' is the making of the essence.

Determination Is Caused by the Locus, Not by a Separate Entity
Proves determination is not caused by a separate entity but by the locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why determination cannot be caused by a separate entity and how it must instead be caused by the locus itself, either directly or indirectly.

Core Idea
No separate entity can specify determination; only the locus can.

In this passage, the author continues his argument about the cause of determination. Having ruled out inherence, he now shows that a separate entity cannot be a specifying cause because its relation to all possibilities is equal. The conclusion is that determination must be caused by the locus itself, a principle that has far-reaching implications for understanding individuality and causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally before you interpret.
2
Identify why a separate entity fails
Notice the key reason: a separate entity has an equal relation to all individuals or essences, so it cannot specify one over another.
The term 'mubayin' includes both abstract and material separate beings.
3
Understand the locus and the circularity response
The passage asserts that the locus is the specifying cause. Then it addresses a potential circularity: inherence depends on individuation, but individuation does not depend on inherence; rather, it depends on the essence itself, similar to hyle being individuated by form.
This response preserves the causal priority of the locus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يعلل أيضاً بما ليس حالاً في الماهية ولا محلاً لها؛ إذ هو مباين عنها نسبته إلى الكل سواء، فلا يمكن أن يكون علة لتعين شخص دون آخر، ولا لتعيين ماهية دون أخرى بل يعلل بمحلها. قوله : (إذ هو مباين عنها سواء كان مجرداً أو مادياً، فلا يمكن أن يكون علة مخصصة لفيضان شخص مخصوص من الفاعل على ماهية دون أخرى . قوله : ( بل يعلل بمحلها أي بل تكون العلة المخصصة محلها إما بنفسه أو بواسطة ما قوله : ( فرع تعينها إلخ) أي يتوقف عليه متأخراً عنه ذاتاً، ولا يكفي المقارنة الزمانية حتى يدفع الدور بها، وقد يجاب بأن حلول شيء في الماهية وإن توقف على تشخصها لكن تشخصها لا يتوقف على حلول ما حل فيه حتى يدور بل على ذاته وهذا بعينه وجه تجويزهم تشخص الهيولى بالصورة الحالة فيها.
And it is also not caused by what is not inherent in the essence nor a locus for it; for it is separate from it, its relation to all is equal, so it cannot be a cause for the determination of one individual over another, nor for the determination of one essence over another. Rather, it is caused by its locus. His saying: (for it is separate from it, whether it is abstract or material, so it cannot be a specifying cause for the flow of a particular individual from the agent upon one essence over another. His saying: (Rather, it is caused by its locus) meaning the specifying cause is its locus, either by itself or by means of something. His saying: (a branch of its determination etc.) means it depends on it, being posterior to it in essence, and temporal concomitance is not sufficient to repudiate the circularity. It may be answered that although the inherence of something in the essence depends on its individuation, yet its individuation does not depend on the inherence of what inheres in it so as to cause circularity, but rather on its essence, and this is precisely the basis for their allowing the individuation of hyle by the form inhering in it.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage completes the disjunctive argument about the cause of determination. After ruling out inherence, the author states that determination is also not caused by something that is neither inherent in the essence nor a locus for it (i.e., a separate entity, mubayin). The reason is that a separate entity—whether abstract (mujarrad) or material—has an equal relation to all possible determinations; it cannot specify one individual or essence over another. Therefore, determination must be caused by the locus (mahall) itself, either directly or indirectly. The commentary clarifies that 'separate' includes both non-material and material beings not inhering in the essence. The specifying cause must be the locus, which is the subject of the essence. The commentary then addresses a potential objection about circularity: it notes that 'branch of its determination' implies ontological posteriority, not merely temporal concomitance. Some respond that although inherence depends on individuation (tashakhkhus), individuation does not depend on that particular inherence; rather, individuation depends on the essence itself. This is analogous to the accepted case of hyle being individuated by the form inhering in it. Thus, determination is from the locus, not from a separate cause.

تشخص
هيولى

Misconception: One might think a separate cause (e.g., an efficient cause or agent) can specify determination because it is powerful.
Correction: The passage argues that a separate entity's relation to all individuals is equal; it cannot specify without a basis in the locus.

Checkpoint

A) Because it is material and cannot affect an immaterial essence.
B) Because its relation to all possible determinations is equal.
C) Because it inherently lacks causal power.
D) Because it is not a locus for the essence.

Key Takeaway
Determination is caused by the locus, not by any separate entity.

Objection and Answer on Circularity Between Locus and Inheriting Accident
Sanusi presents an objection about circularity between the individuation of locus and inhering accident, and answers it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circularity objection against the individuation of the locus by an inheriting accident and how the answer refutes it by denying the premise that the accident's individuation comes from the locus.

Core Idea
Circularity objections only work if you assume the very point in dispute.

This passage presents a classic kalam objection: if a locus is individuated by an accident inhering in it, then the accident's own individuation seemingly must come from the locus, creating a vicious circle. Sanusi answers by showing that the objector assumes the accident's individuation depends on the locus, which is precisely what is contested. Let's examine the argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the structure: 'fa-in qulta' introduces the objection, and 'qultu' introduces the answer.
2
Understand the objection
Identify the two dependencies claimed: the locus's individuation depends on the accident's individuation, and the accident's individuation depends on the locus. Why would these lead to circularity?
The objector says making an ambiguous essence a cause of individuation is meaningless.
3
Analyze the answer
Sanusi denies that the accident's individuation must come from the locus. He states that this claim is based on an assumption that is not accepted—it is 'the very point at issue' (huwa awwal al-mas'alah).
The answer refutes by showing question-begging.
4
Reflect on the fallacy
Consider why the objection is circular reasoning: it assumes the dependency it tries to prove. The answer breaks the circle by denying that dependency.
This is a common dialectical move in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : تشخص المحل حينئذ يتوقف على تشخص الحال إذ لا معنى لجعل الذات المبهمة علة للتشخص، وتشخص الحال إنما هو من المحل فيدور، قلت : كون تشخص الحال من المحل مبني على عدم جواز كونه مما حل فيه للزوم الدور، وهو أول المسألة.
If you say: Then the individuation of the locus depends on the individuation of the inheriting accident, for it is meaningless to make the ambiguous essence a cause of individuation, and the individuation of the inheriting accident comes only from the locus, leading to circularity. I say: The fact that the individuation of the inheriting accident is from the locus is based on the impossibility of it being from what inheres in it due to the necessity of circularity, and that is the very point at issue.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair. The objector raises a circularity problem: If the locus (mahall) is individuated by something inhering in it (the accidental form), then that inheriting accident's own individuation must come from the locus (since it inheres in it). This creates a circular dependency: the locus's individuation depends on the accident's individuation, and vice versa. The objector argues that making an indeterminate essence into a cause of individuation is meaningless, so there is no way out. The answer (qultu) states that the very claim that the inheriting accident's individuation comes from the locus is based on the assumption that it cannot come from something else that inheres in it—because that would lead to the same circularity. But the point is that we do not accept that assumption; rather, the accident's individuation can come from its own essence or from a different source. Thus, the objection assumes the very thing under dispute (huwa awwal al-mas'alah). In other words, the objector begs the question by assuming that the accident's individuation must come from the locus, which is exactly what is being argued against. The answer refutes the circularity by denying the dependency.

Key Terms
تشخص
محل
حال
دور
ذات مبهمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if the locus is individuated by an inhering accident, then the accident's individuation must come from the locus.
Correction: The answer shows that this dependency is not necessary; the accident's individuation can come from its own essence or another source, breaking the circularity.

Checkpoint
In the objection, why does the objector think circularity occurs?
A) Because the locus individuates the accident and the accident individuates the locus.
B) Because the agent is required for both.
C) Because the locus is ambiguous and cannot cause anything.
D) Because the accident is separate from the locus.

Key Takeaway
The answer refutes the circularity objection by pointing out that it assumes the accident's individuation depends on the locus, which is precisely the point under dispute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The objector’s argument seemed logical, yet it was built on an unproven assumption. Are there areas of your faith where you have accepted something as true simply because it fits your existing framework, without checking whether it is actually proven? Will you challenge one such assumption today?
?
This passage shows how easy it is to beg the question. In your daily life, when you feel certain about something, how often do you pause to ask: 'Is this belief based on evidence, or am I assuming what I want to be true?' What practical step can you take to ensure your certainty is grounded in truth, not circular reasoning?

Two Ways of Multiplicity Through Receptive Subjects
Classifies three scenarios of individual multiplicity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the multiplicity of individuals arises either by intrinsic multiplicity of the receptive subject or by accidental predispositions, and when it is confined to one.

Core Idea
Individual multiplicity is always due to the receptive subject—either by essence or accident.

This passage from al-Mawaqif explains the root cause of why there are multiple individuals of the same essence. The author first states a general principle: multiplicity comes from the receptive subject (qabil). He then gives two distinct ways this happens—by the subject's own nature or by surrounding accidents—and also notes when multiplicity is absent. This foundation is essential for understanding the subsequent conclusion about non-material beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's classification come through.
The passage uses technical terms like qawabil and isti'dadat.
2
Identify the two types of multiplicity
Find the two ways multiplicity occurs: by essence (bi al-dhat) and by accidents. Note the examples given for each.
3
Understand the confinement case
Notice the third scenario when neither type applies: the essence is confined to a single individual. The example is the hyle of a single sphere.
This sets up the later argument about non-material beings.
4
Connect to broader kalam theory
Consider why this classification matters: it underlies the principle that multiplicity requires a receptive substrate.
This is a key premise for the uniqueness of immaterial intellects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعددها أي تعدد أفرادها) بتعدد القوابل) أي المحال (إما بالذات) كهيولات الأفلاك القابلة لصورها الجسمية وكالنطف القابلة للصورة الإنسانية . ( وإما بسبب أعراض تكتنفها كهيولى العناصر الأربعة، فإنها واحدة مشتركة بينها، وقد عرض لها استعدادات مختلفة بحسب القرب والبعد من الفلك، فلذلك تعدد أشخاصها . وإذا لم يتعدد القابل بالذات ولم يتصور فيها استعدادات متفاوتة انحصرت الماهية الحالة في شخص واحد أيضا كهيولى كل فلك بالقياس إلى صورته النوعية . ( وبنوا على هذا الذي ذكروه من أن تعدد أفراد الماهية الواحد إنما يكون بتعدد قابلها، أعني مادتها على أحد الوجهين أن ما ليس بمادي ويسمي مجرداً ومفارقاً، فنوعه منحصر في الشخص الواحد ؛ لأن علة تعينه ليست المحل، إذ لا محل لغير المادي، فهي إما الماهية نفسها أو ما يلزمها فيلزم الانحصار كما مر . وقد يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يكون للمجرد محل غير المادة الجسمية فيتعدد بتعدد ذلك المحل، إما ذاتاً أو استعداداً يحل فيه، كما يدل عليه قوله : وأما بسبب أعراض إلخ، فلا يرد أن هاهنا قسماً آخر وهو أن يعلل بما يحل في محلها.
Its multiplicity (i.e., multiplicity of its individuals) is by the multiplicity of receptive subjects, i.e., the loci, either by essence (dhat), like the hyle of celestial spheres receptive to their corporeal forms, and like the sperm receptive to the human form; or due to accidents surrounding them, like the hyle of the four elements, which is one common to them, but it has different predispositions according to nearness and distance from the celestial sphere, so their individuals become multiple. And if the receptive subject is not multiple by essence and no varying predispositions are conceived in it, the inhering essence is confined to a single individual as well, like the hyle of each celestial sphere in relation to its specific form. And they built upon this that the multiplicity of individuals of a single essence is only by the multiplicity of its receptive subject, i.e., its matter, in one of the two ways: that which is not material and is called abstract (mujarrad) and separate (mufariq) — its species is confined to a single individual, because the cause of its determination is not the locus, since there is no locus for the non-material; rather it is either the essence itself or what accompanies it, so confinement follows as before. And it may be said: Why is it not permissible for the abstract to have a locus other than bodily matter, so that it becomes multiple by the multiplicity of that locus, either by essence or by predisposition that inheres in it, as indicated by his saying: 'And due to accidents surrounding them'? Then it would not be refuted that there is another division: that it is caused by what inheres in its locus.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents a classification and a conclusion about the cause of individual multiplicity. It first states that the multiplicity of individuals of a single essence is due to the multiplicity of receptive subjects (qawabil or mahall). This multiplicity occurs in two ways: (1) by essence, as in the hyle of celestial spheres which are distinct by nature and receive different forms, or sperm receiving a human form; (2) due to accidents surrounding the receptive subject, as in the case of the hyle of the four elements—the hyle is one but gains different predispositions (isti'dadat) based on proximity or distance from the celestial sphere, leading to multiple individuals. If neither intrinsic multiplicity nor varying dispositions exist, the inhering essence is confined to one individual, like the hyle of a single celestial sphere relative to its specific form. Building on this, the author concludes that any non-material being (mujarrad/mufariq) has its species confined to a single individual. The reason: since it has no matter, its cause of determination cannot be a locus; it must be either the essence itself or a necessary concomitant (lazim), which leads to singularity. The passage then raises an objection: could an abstract being have a locus other than bodily matter—perhaps a non-material substrate? If so, it could multiply by that substrate's multiplicity. The objector suggests this is implied by the previous classification (due to accidents). The author likely dismisses this, but the text cuts off. The phrase 'as indicated by his saying...' suggests that the objection is based on a misinterpretation of the earlier point about accidents. The final line notes that another division would not be refuted: determination caused by what inheres in its locus. This passage is crucial for the kalam theory of individuation.

محال
استعدادات

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of multiplicity due to accidents?
A) Sperm receiving human form
B) Hyle of celestial spheres
C) Hyle of elements gaining different predispositions
D) Hyle of each sphere with its specific form

Key Takeaway
Multiplicity of individuals is always caused by multiplicity in the receptive subject, either by its nature or by accidental predispositions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your soul is a receptive subject for knowledge of God. According to this lesson, its capacity to receive truth is shaped either by its essence or by accidental circumstances (like environment and effort). Which is shaping your receptivity today? What one change can you make this week to improve your predisposition to receive divine guidance?
?
The passage says that when predispositions do not vary, the essence is confined to one individual. If you find yourself stuck in spiritual stagnation, is it because you have let your predispositions become fixed? How will you intentionally introduce variation—through new knowledge, sincere supplication, or companionship of the righteous—so that your soul becomes receptive to more of God's light?

Non-Material Substances Have Single Individuals
Concludes non-material species have single individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why non-material (abstract) beings have only one individual per species, based on their lack of matter.

Core Idea
Non-material species are confined to one individual because determination cannot come from a locus.

Building on the previous principle, the author now applies it to non-material beings. Since these beings have no matter, they lack a receptive subject that could serve as the basis for multiple individuals. Therefore, each species of non-material being (like angels or intellects) consists of a single individual. This passage explains the reasoning behind that conclusion and anticipates a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Read and understand the conclusion
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that the conclusion is: non-material species have only one individual.
The term 'mujarrad' or 'mufariq' means abstract / separate.
2
Analyze the reasoning
The reasoning: multiplicity requires matter (receptive subject); non-material has no matter; therefore no multiplicity; thus one individual per species.
The cause of determination (ta'ayyun) is also discussed.
3
See how it follows from the previous classification
This is a direct application of the earlier principle: if no receptive subject, no multiplicity.
The author says 'they built upon this'.

Commentary

It first states that the multiplicity of individuals of a single essence is due to the multiplicity of receptive subjects (qawabil or mahall). Misconception: Non-material beings can have multiple individuals if they have different essences.

Why does the author conclude that a non-material species has only one individual?

Non-material beings lack matter, so they cannot have multiple individuals within one species.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The angels are non-material and each angelic species is a single individual. Consider the angels who record your deeds—each one is unique. Does this give you a deeper sense of accountability for your actions?
?
If God is not a species and is absolutely unique, how does the confinement of non-material species to one individual help you appreciate the uniqueness of God? What does it demand from you in worship?

Objection Against Non-Material Multiplicity
Presents objection and partial response about non-material loci.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that abstract beings might have a non-material locus, leading to multiplicity, and how the author counters it.

Core Idea
An abstract being cannot have any locus, not even a non-material one.

The author anticipates an objection to the previous conclusion: could a non-material being have a non-material locus that is multiple, thus allowing multiple individuals? The objector points to the earlier case of accidents causing multiplicity in material beings and suggests a similar possibility for abstract beings. This passage presents the objection and the beginning of a response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage. It starts with 'And it may be said' (wa qad yuqal).
The objection challenges the conclusion about non-material beings.
2
Understand the analogy to accidents
The objector refers to the earlier case where accidents cause multiplicity. He suggests that if an abstract being could have a non-material locus with dispositions, it could become multiple.
The objector says 'as indicated by his saying: And due to accidents...'
3
Identify the author's response (fragmentary)
The response begins with 'fa-la yurad anna hahuna qisman akhar...' meaning 'then it would not be refuted that there is another division...' The full response is cut off but indicates a rebuttal.
The author likely argues that determination cannot come from a locus if the locus itself is non-material.
4
Reflect on why this objection fails
Consider that the cause of determination for non-material beings must be their essence, not any external locus.
This reinforces the earlier conclusion.

Causality and Created Things

Why Human Souls Are Multiple Despite Immateriality
Commentator explains multiplicity of human souls despite immateriality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument for why human souls are multiple despite being immaterial, based on their attachment to matter through governance and mastery, and how this differs from the attachment of intellects.

Core Idea
Immaterial souls are multiple because they govern diverse bodies, not because they are material.

The commentator addresses a critical objection in Islamic philosophy: if human souls are immaterial, they should be numerically one. The answer lies in the nature of their attachment to bodies—not as material constituents but as governors. This lesson unpacks the detailed explanation, including the Peripatetic basis and the distinction from intellects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first part where the objection is posed: if souls are immaterial, how can they be multiple? Notice the commentator's framing.
The objection assumes immaterial entities are unique in species.
2
Understand the core answer
Focus on the phrase 'لتعلقها بالمادة تعلق التدبير والتصرف'. This attachment makes souls like material things in terms of multiplicity.
Attachment via governance, not subsistence in matter.
3
Examine the Peripatetic basis
The commentator relates this to the Peripatetic view that souls agree in specific essence but differ due to bodily temperaments.
Each body requires a specific soul tailored to its temperament.
4
Contrast with intellects
Read the part about 'بخلاف العقول'. Intellects are attached via influence (ta'theer) and are prior in existence, so they are not multiple.
Intellects are efficient causes, not governors.
5
Reflect on celestial souls
The commentator discusses whether celestial souls are of one species or multiple. Consider the two possibilities presented.
The attachment to matter permits both unity and multiplicity of species.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد الثاني عشر : التعين إن علل بالماهية

ولما كان لقائل أن يقول : النفوس الناطقة متعددة مع كونها مجردة عندهم أجاب بقوله : ( والنفوس الإنسانية إنما تعددت وإن لم تكن (مادية) أي حالة في المادة ( لتعلقها بالمادة تعلق التدبير والتصرف، فهي في حكم الماديات، فتتعدد بحسب تعدد المادة التي تتعلق بها، بخلاف العقول المجردة عن المادة بحسب الذات والتعلق فإن أنواعها منحصرة في أشخاصها . ( قال بعض الفضلاء ) : إذا كان تعين الماهية المتعددة الأفراد معللا ،بالقابل ) فالقابل إن كان تشخصه بماهيته أو لوازمها ( انحصر نوعه في شخصه، ولم يقولوا به أي بكون تعينه معللاً بماهيته وانحصاره في

قوله: (النفوس الناطقة إلخ) بناء على ما ذهب إليه المشاؤون من كونها متفقة بحسب الماهية النوعية .

قوله : ( لتعلقها إلخ) أي بالأبدان تعلق التدبير ولما كانت الأبدان متخالفة بحسب الأمزجة لا بد لكل واحد في تدبيره من مدبر خاص يدبره على نحو ما يليق به، فبسبب ذلك المزاج الخاص اقتضى كل بدن نفساً مخصوصة فكانت في حكم الماديات في أن تشخص أفرادها بسبب استعدادات حصلت في ،أبدانها ومن هذا ظهر الفرق بينها وبين العقول، فإنها متقدمة بحسب الوجود والتشخص لكونها عللاً مؤثرة.

قوله : ( والنفوس الإنسانية إنما تعددت إلخ) تقييد النفوس بالإنسانية يشعر بأن النفوس الفلكية مختلفة بالنوع مع تعلقها بالمواد الفلكية تعلق التدبير والتصرف. والحق أن هذه النفوس من حيث تعلقها بالمواد تحتمل الاتحاد النوعي كالنفوس الإنسانية، وتعدد المواد الفلكية ذاتاً لا يقدح فيه ؛ لجواز أن يتعلق بكل منها فرد من ماهية نوعية نفسية كما يتعلق بكل منها فرد من نوع الصورة الجسمية وتحتمل الاختلاف النوعي، إذ التعلق بالمواد مجوز للاختلاف الشخصي للماهية النوعية لا مناف للاختلاف النوعي . قوله : (بخلاف العقول إلخ) فإن قلت العقول أيضاً متعلقة بالمادة وإن كان تعلق التأثير وما الفرق بين التعلقين قلت : تعلق التأثير يستدعي تقدم المؤثر بالوجود والتشخص؛ ولو ذاتاً، فلا معنى لإسناد تشخصه إلى المتأثر المتأخر، وأما تعلق التدبير والتصرف فلا يستدعي تقدم تشخص المدبر على ذات المدبر فيه وإن استدعى تقدمه على التدبير فلا محذور فيه فليتأمل
Second Observation - Twelfth Topic: Determination if it is caused by the essence. And since it is possible for someone to say: the rational souls are multiple while being immaterial according to them, he answered by his saying: (And the human souls are multiple only, even if they are not material, i.e., subsisting in matter, because of their attachment to matter with the attachment of governance and mastery, so they are in the ruling of material things, so they become multiple according to the multiplicity of the matter to which they are attached, unlike the intellects that are abstracted from matter in terms of essence and attachment, for their species are confined to their individuals. (Some virtuous one said): If the determination of the essence having multiple individuals is caused by the recipient, then if the recipient's individuation is by its essence or its necessary concomitants, its species would be restricted to its individual, and they do not say that, i.e., that its determination is caused by its essence and its restriction to... His saying: (the rational souls, etc.) is based on what the Peripatetics went to of their agreement in specific essence. His saying: (their attachment, etc.) means to the bodies with the attachment of governance, and since the bodies differ according to temperaments, each one must have a particular governor who governs it in a way suitable to it, so because of that particular temperament, each body necessitated a particular soul, so they were in the ruling of material things in that their individuals are individuated due to preparations that occurred in their bodies, and from this the difference between them and the intellects appears, for they (intellects) are prior in existence and individuation because they are efficient causes. His saying: (And the human souls are multiple, etc.) The restriction of souls to 'human' indicates that the celestial souls are different in species while being attached to celestial matters with the attachment of governance and mastery. The truth is that these souls, in terms of their attachment to matters, could be of one species like human souls, and the multiplicity of the celestial matters in themselves does not harm that; because it is possible that an individual from a psychic specific essence attaches to each of them, just as an individual from the type of corporeal form attaches to each of them. And they could be different in species, because attachment to matters permits personal difference for the specific essence, not prevents specific difference. His saying: (unlike the intellects, etc.) For if you say: the intellects are also attached to matter, even if it is the attachment of influence, and what is the difference between the two attachments? I say: The attachment of influence necessitates the priority of the influencer in existence and individuation, even if in essence, so there is no meaning to attributing its individuation to the affected thing that is subsequent. As for the attachment of governance and mastery, it does not necessitate the priority of the individuation of the governor over the essence of the thing governed, even if it necessitates its priority over the governance, so there is no problem in it. So reflect.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection regarding the multiplicity of human souls. It begins by stating the objection: if souls are immaterial, they should not be multiple. The answer is that human souls, though immaterial in essence, are attached to matter in the mode of governance and mastery, so they are treated like material things and become multiple due to the multiplicity of the bodies they govern. The commentator then explains that this is based on the Peripatetic view that human souls agree in specific essence but differ due to the different temperaments of bodies, each requiring a particular soul. The distinction from intellects is made: intellects are separate from matter both in essence and in attachment, so their species coincides with their individuals. The passage further addresses celestial souls, noting that the restriction 'human' implies celestial souls may differ in species despite attachment to celestial matter. However, it allows for both possibilities: they could be of one species like human souls, or of different species. Finally, it clarifies the difference between two types of attachment: the attachment of influence (ta'theer), which requires the influencer to be prior, and the attachment of governance (tadbir), which does not require such priority, thus explaining why intellects remain one in species while human souls are multiple.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since human souls are immaterial, they must be of one species and not multiple.
Correction: Immateriality does not preclude multiplicity if the souls are attached to matter via governance, as their individuation depends on the bodies they govern.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between human souls and intellects according to the passage?
A) Human souls are material while intellects are immaterial.
B) Human souls are attached to matter by governance, while intellects are attached by influence and are prior in existence.
C) Human souls have multiple species, while intellects have one species.
D) Human souls are caused by bodies, while intellects are not.

Key Takeaway
Human souls are multiple because their attachment to bodies via governance makes them like material things, unlike intellects which are attached via influence and are prior in existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your soul is uniquely tied to your body, governing it through every action you take. In what areas are you allowing your body to lead your soul instead of the other way around? Commit to one specific change today that realigns your governance.
?
The intellects are pure causes, detached from matter, while your soul is engaged with the world through governance. Have you ever attributed to yourself the role of 'cause' in your life, forgetting that you are merely a governor over what Allah has given you? Where do you need to surrender that illusion of control?
?
If your soul is individuated by the specific body and temperament you have been given, what unique responsibility does that place on you before Allah? What good or harm are you uniquely capable of that no one else can do? Write down one concrete way you will fulfill that responsibility this week.

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
6 min
Introduction to Determination of the Recipient
Commentator explains the two possibilities for determination and states the philosophers' doctrine on hayula's individuation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible causes of determination for a recipient and the philosophers' view that hayula is individuated by form, not by its own essence.

Core Idea
Hayula is individuated by form, not by its essence.

This lesson introduces the problem of determination (ta'ayyun) for a recipient that can have multiple individuals. The commentators explain that determination must come from either the essential (malzum) or the concomitant (lazim). The philosophers, however, maintain that prime matter (hayula) is not determined by its own essence but by the form that inheres in it. This sets the stage for a deeper discussion on causality and specification.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
The passage begins with an explanation of a pronoun reference, but quickly moves to the key point: the philosophers' view on hayula's individuation. Read carefully to grasp the two possibilities.
The pronoun 'bi-hi' is ambiguous; the commentator clarifies why it refers to both malzum and lazim.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage states that determination is either by the necessary (malzum) or its concomitant (lazim). Note how the commentator argues against exclusive reference.
3
Focus on the core doctrine
The crucial line is 'بل تعينه عندهم بصورته' – rather, its determination is by its form. This is the philosophers' position that hayula is individuated by form, not essence.
This contradicts the idea that essence alone suffices for individuation.
4
Reflect on the significance
This shows that the recipient (qabil) cannot be individuated by its essence alone, opening questions about the role of forms in causality and specification.
The passage hints at a larger debate on whether essence can be individuated by what inheres in it.

قوله : ( معلل بالصورة (الحالة قال المحقق في شرح الإشارات الهيولى إنما تصير هذه الهيولى بعينها لأجل صورة تعينها لا من حيث إنها هذه الصورة بل من حيث إنها صورة ما . وتفصيله ما قاله الإمام في المباحث المشرقية المؤثر في وجود الهيولى المعينة هو وجود المفارق وهو شيء معين الذات مثل تعين ذات الهيولى المعينة وأما الصورة فإنها كما عرفت شرائط لوصول تأثير المفارق والحاجة إلى الصورة ليست من حيث هي تلك الصورة، بل من حيث إنها صورة ما . والمعلول المعين الشخصي وإن كان يستدعي علة معينة شخصية، ولكن لا يستدعي أن تكون شرائط التأثير أموراً بأعيانها. انتهى. وبما نقلنا ظهر أن الصورة المطلقة شريكة فاعل الهيولى المعينة وأنها معتبرة في جانب الفاعل وليست مخصصة للهيولى يتعين دون آخر لأن الصورة المطلقة لا دخل لها في التخصيص، وكلامنا في العلة المخصصة، بل مخصصها بتعين دون آخر ذاتها وأن هيولى كل فلك وهيولى العناصر نوعها منحصر في فرد فاندفع إيراد بعض الفضلاء بالنظر إلى نفس الهيولى وأما بالنظر إلى تعدد أشخاصها باعتبار تبعضها، وحصصها باعتبار أشخاص الأجسام العنصرية وباعتبار أشخاص خوارج المراكز والتداوير والكواكب، فيسيجيء أنه باعتبار العوارض المكتنفة بها، وكذا اندفع ما ذكره الشارح قدس سره بقوله : ومن هاهنا يظهر جواز إلخ لأن علية الصورة من حيث ذاتها لا من حيث حلولها، ولأنها ليست مخصصة والكلام في المخصص.

His saying: (i.e., it is, etc.) i.e., by something from the necessary and its concomitant. As for the first, it is due to his saying: 'rather its determination' etc. As for the second, because their doctrine is that the elemental individuals share in hayula, and that the individuals of the partial spheres from the centers, epicycles, and planets share in the hayula of the universal sphere. The pronoun in 'bi-hi' is not referred only to the concomitant to avoid repulsion from it, nor only to the necessary to avoid needing to mention the concomitant afterwards. His saying: (i.e., its determination being caused by its essence and its restriction to one individual) is a reference to the fact that his intention is not to assert the combination, as is apparent from his expression, but not asserting it is by virtue of not asserting the part of the first, as indicated by his saying: 'rather its determination according to them is by its form', so it does not contradict what is well-known from them of saying the unity of the hayula of the elements. Second Observation - Twelfth Topic: Determination if it is caused by the essence. One individual, rather its determination according to them is by its form; because the individuation of hayula is caused according to them by the form inhering in it, not by the essence of hayula. And from here appears the permissibility of the individuation of an essence by what inheres in it, and they built their argument on the impermissibility of it) And if the individuation of the recipient by what inheres in it were necessary... It would suffice then to say: If its individuation is by its essence, they do not say it, so understand, for it is a place where feet slip. His saying: (caused by the form (inhering) al-Muhaqqiq said in Sharh al-Isharat: Hayula only becomes this particular hayula because of a form determining it, not in that it is this form, but in that it is a form. Its detail is what the Imam said in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya: The effective cause in the existence of the determined hayula is the existence of the separate being, and it is something determined in essence like the determination of the essence of the determined hayula. As for the form, it is, as you have known, conditions for the arrival of the influence of the separate being, and the need for a form is not in it being that particular form, but in it being a form. And the determined personal effect, even if it requires a determined personal cause, does not require that the conditions of influence be specific things. End. And from what we have transmitted, it appears that the absolute form is a partner of the agent of the determined hayula, and it is considered on the side of the agent, and it is not a specifier of hayula to become determined rather than another, because the absolute form has no role in specification. Our discussion is about the specifying cause. Rather, its specifier to determination rather than another is its essence, and that the hayula of each sphere and the hayula of the elements have their species confined to one individual. Thus the objection of some virtuous one with respect to the hayula itself is repelled. As for with respect to the multiplicity of its individuals through its division and its shares through the individuals of elemental bodies and through the individuals of the centers, epicycles, and planets, it will come that it is through the surrounding accidents. Similarly, what the commentator (may his secret be sanctified) mentioned by his saying: 'And from here appears the permissibility, etc.' is repelled, because the causality of the form is from its essence, not from its inherence, and because it is not a specifier, and the discussion is about the specifier. The elements. An individual, and it might be said that their intention by the unity of the hayula of the elements as an individual is that it is one individual with no separation in its essence, and it is only from outside and by it it becomes multiple individuals. Perhaps it is claimed that their intention by unity is specific unity, and the addition of individuation is an interpretation of the transmitter according to his understanding. This is indicated by their explicit statement of the multiplicity of its individuals due to nearness and distance from the sphere, as has passed recently. His saying: (rather its determination according to them is by its form) contains discussion; because this contradicts the famous, and it will also come in the station of substance: namely that hayula is in need of form for its survival, and form is in need of it for its determination. It might be answered: There is no contradiction between the two needs, so it is possible that hayula's need of form is for survival and individuation together, and there is no problem in each of them needing the other's essence for individuation, as the Imam stated in Sharh al-Isharat. It was said: The verification is that the individuation of the form is by the determined hayula being receptive to its individuation, and the individuation of hayula is by the absolute form as it is an agent for its individuation. And we say: The commentator will indicate the falsity of this verification in the station of substance where he said: We said: the one is...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the determination (ta'ayyun) of the recipient (qabil) and the role of form (surah) in individuating hayula (prime matter). It begins by explaining a prior statement: the determination of an essence with multiple individuals is caused either by something from the necessary (malzum) or its concomitant (lazim). The commentator clarifies that the philosophers do not hold that the determination of the recipient is by its essence, because they believe hayula is determined by the form inhering in it. The passage then cites al-Muhaqqiq (Nasir al-Din al-Tusi) and Imam al-Razi to argue that hayula becomes this particular hayula not because of the specific form, but because of form in general, which serves as a condition for the influence of the separate being (al-mufariq). The absolute form is not a specifier (mukhasis); the true specifier is the separate being's essence or the essence of hayula itself. The refutation of an objection by 'some virtuous one' is presented, showing that the form is a partner in the agent side and not a specifier. The passage also addresses the unity of the hayula of the elements, discussing whether it is numerically one or specifically one. Finally, a caution is given against a famous view that form is determined by hayula and vice versa, with a promise of further discussion in the station of substance.

Key Takeaway
The philosopher's position is that prime matter (hayula) is individuated by the form that inheres in it, not by its own essence.

Causality and Created Things

8 min
Form as Condition, Not Specifier
Commentator cites authorities to prove that form is a condition for influence, not a specifier of hayula.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument from al-Muhaqqiq and Imam al-Razi that form serves as a condition for the influence of the separate being, not as a specifier of hayula.

Core Idea
Absolute form is a condition for influence, not a specifier of hayula.

This lesson delves into the detailed argument that the form (surah) is not the specifying cause (mukhasis) of hayula, but rather a condition (shart) for the influence of the separate being (al-mufariq). The passage cites al-Muhaqqiq (Nasir al-Din al-Tusi) and Imam al-Razi to support this, emphasizing that the absolute form is a partner in the agent side, not a specifier.

Guided Path
1
Read the citation from al-Muhaqqiq
The passage quotes al-Muhaqqiq from Sharh al-Isharat, stating that hayula becomes this particular hayula because of a form, not in that it is this form but in that it is a form. This is key.
The form is considered generally, not specifically.
2
Understand al-Razi's detail
Imam al-Razi in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya explains that the effective cause of determined hayula is a separate being (mufariq), and the form is a condition for its influence. The need for form is not for a specific form but for form in general.
The influence reaches hayula through the form as a condition.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The absolute form is a partner of the agent, not a specifier. Specification (takhsis) is done by the essence of the separate being or of hayula itself.
The passage explicitly says: 'الصورة المطلقة لا دخل لها في التخصيص'.
